The temperature data for AWOS sites represent the highest and

lowest temperatures that were reported on the metar observations

that transmit three times an hour and may not represent the actual

high or low for that site.  These sites do not measure precipitation.



These data are preliminary and have not undergone final quality

control by the National Centers for Environmental Information /NCEI/.

Therefore these data are subject to revision.  Final and certified

climate data can be accessed at www.ncei.noaa.gov

Fire Weather Planning Forecast for Hawaii

National Weather Service Honolulu HI

300 AM HST Sat Nov 4 2023



...FIRE WEATHER WATCH IN EFFECT FROM SUNDAY MORNING THROUGH

MONDAY AFTERNOON...

...NEAR CRITICAL WIND AND RELATIVE HUMIDITY TODAY...





.DISCUSSION...

Breezy trade winds today and tonight, will become windy and very

gusty Sunday through Monday. The trades will ease back to breezy

levels Tuesday through late next week. Rather dry trade wind 

weather will prevail through the majority of the weekend, after a 

showery start this morning for windward sections of the smaller 

islands. A dissipating front will gradually sag southward into the

smaller islands early next week, bringing a showery pattern to 

windward areas and sending a few showers into leeward communities 

as well. Fairly typical trade wind weather is then expected 

statewide Wednesday through late next week.



Strong winds and low humidity levels, combined with dry fuels 

will bring dangerous fire weather conditions Sunday and Monday. A 

Fire Weather Watch remains in effect for all leeward zones as well

as central Oahu, and this watch will likely need to be upgraded 

to a Red Flag Warning later today.

MORNING THROUGH MONDAY AFTERNOON...



.Dry fuels combined with strong trade winds and lowering 

humidities could produce critical fire weather conditions from 

Sunday morning through Monday afternoon.



HIZ201-203-205>208-210-211-213>215-218-219-221-223-224-226-227-

050400-

/O.CON.PHFO.FW.A.0004.231105T2000Z-231107T0400Z/

Niihau-Kauai Leeward-Oahu South Shore-Waianae Coast-

Oahu North Shore-Oahu Koolau-Central Oahu-Waianae Mountains-

Molokai Leeward-Lanai Makai-Lanai Mauka-Maui Leeward West-

Maui Central Valley-Leeward Haleakala-Kona-South Big Island-

Kohala-Big Island Interior-

300 AM HST Sat Nov 4 2023



...FIRE WEATHER WATCH REMAINS IN EFFECT FROM SUNDAY MORNING

THROUGH MONDAY AFTERNOON FOR WIND AND LOW RELATIVE HUMIDITY FOR

ALL LEEWARD AREAS AND FOR CENTRAL OAHU...



* AFFECTED AREA...Leeward areas of all Hawaiian Islands and 

  central Oahu. 



* TIMING...From Sunday morning through Monday afternoon.



* WINDS...East 20 to 30 mph with gusts up to 45 mph.



* RELATIVE HUMIDITY...35 to 40 percent Sunday afternoon and 

  40 to 45 percent Monday afternoon. 



* IMPACTS...A combination of strong winds, low relative 

  humidity,and dry fuels can contribute to extreme fire 

  behavior. Any fires that develop could spread rapidly. A Fire 

  Weather Watch does not predict the potential for new fire 

  starts. 



PRECAUTIONARY/PREPAREDNESS ACTIONS...



Should a Red Flag warning be issued, outdoor burning is not

recommended.



It is recommended to delay activities that could throw off sparks

until the wind dies down.



A Fire Weather Watch means that critical fire weather conditions

are forecast to occur. Listen for later forecasts and possible

Red Flag Warnings.



&&



For actions you can take to protect life and property from

wildfires, visit the Hawaii Wildfire Management Organization at

https://www.hawaiiwildfire.org/home

FXUS61 KGYX 061215

AFDGYX



Area Forecast Discussion

National Weather Service Gray ME

715 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023



.SYNOPSIS...

The high pressure that has brought so much fair weather will

begin to drift east Monday, allowing clouds to fill in from the

west through the day. A stronger system will move through Canada

Tuesday, leading to showery weather as it crosses. More notably

is that it will drive a cold front through the region bringing

in a cooler, drier, and gustier air mass that lingers into

Wednesday. The next chance of precipitation arrives late in the

week, and while it looks mostly wet it is worth keeping an eye

on for wintry precipitation types.



&&



.NEAR TERM /UNTIL 6 PM THIS EVENING/...

7am Update...Mainly just some adjustments to morning

temperatures. Great cooling across the interior last night with

many locations experiencing a hard freeze with lows in the mid

to lower 20s. Some stubborn stratus held on across the seacoast

of NH, allowing more mild temps there in the mid to upper 30s. 



Previous Discussion...

High pressure ridging peaks today with fair conditions and 

light winds. After a chilly night, highs today won't rebound too

much. Highs stick mainly in the lower to mid 40s as cloud cover

begins to increase around peak heating and through the second 

half of the day.



Will generally see these cloud bases lowering into the evening

amid onshore flow. The return flow behind the high will be

strong, and winds will likely be on the increase late this

afternoon into the overnight hours.



&&



.SHORT TERM /6 PM THIS EVENING THROUGH 6 PM TUESDAY/...

This flow will provide much of the area with mild WAA. Locations

in the southern half of NH and across coastal/interior ME will

see this anti-diurnal trend through the evening and overnight.

Temps may only fluctuate a couple degrees here from noon Monday

to midnight. Further warming will be possible during the late

night hours as low pressure passes into southern Quebec.



Precipitation will overspread the area late this evening

associated with this low. Overall, light QPF trend remains, and

have continued to adjust amounts down. Continue to see a

gradient of a few tenths of precipitation in central Maine to a

few hundredths in southern NH. Higher terrain points will see 

the greatest amounts, but generally fall below a half inch 

total. Rain will be the primary precip type. The only exception 

looks to be a rain/snow mix in the mountains and valleys of 

northern NH and western ME tonight. Profiles are warm however, 

and don't expect ratios higher than 5:1 resulting in wet flakes.

Otherwise, warm air should swap much of this over to a rain 

event through Tuesday.



Winds will be gusty in the warm sector overnight and into the

morning. Gusts to 25 mph will be possible in the lowlands, with

a brief visit to triple digit readings possible atop the 

Rockpile. Gale conditions will be possible over the waters early

Tuesday morning.



Much of the steady precip tapers Tuesday morning, with showers

continuing amid a W wind shift. These will be most prevalent in

the mountains. However, the cold front will come crashing

through the CWA during Tuesday afternoon. There will be a brief

period of enhanced low level lapse rates and therefore

instability to reinvigorate of showers across the interior. 

There may be enough MUCAPE for a few of these showers to contain

graupel as they pass from the mountains to the coast. These 

taper off in the mid to late afternoon with weak sun angle 

decreasing avail instability.



&&



.LONG TERM /TUESDAY NIGHT THROUGH SUNDAY/...

Overview: Largely zonal flow will keep systems moving fast and

impacts locally defined mainly by timing of each individual

wave. Reinforcing cold fronts will keep temps mostly cooler than

normal.



Impacts: With cold air nearby...any well timed wave may lead to

wintry precip types.



Forecast Details: Post-frontal CAA Wed will keep gusty winds

going and cool temps across the forecast area. Temps will likely

end up significant colder north and west of the mtns...where

upslope cloud cover will limit mixing. By late in the day or

during the evening...heights will begin rising and at least S/WV

ridging attempts to cross the region. This will bring an end to

upslope snow showers



Seasonably cool weather continues thru the end of the week...and

leads to an interesting signal Thu into Fri. The next S/WV trof

passes the area...but model guidance is all over the place in

how it is being handled. Most operational models have some sort

of flat wave that brings some rain and a wintry mix to parts of

the area. However the ECMWF EPS EFI shows a band of high shift

of tails near the coast for snowfall despite no EFI value. That

says that the top 10 percent of ensemble members are showing a 

noteworthy snowfall for this time of year. Digging a little 

deeper using DESI...the mean/median comparison of all ensemble 

members confirms what the ECMWF is showing. The mean has up to a

few inches of snowfall across the interior portions of the

forecast area...while the median is zero just about everywhere.

So it is a small handful of members dragging the mean up. So

with the threat being around a 1 in 10 chance...it is worth

keeping an eye on...but not worth putting into the forecast

currently.



Otherwise there was not much change from previous forecasts.



&&



.AVIATION /12Z MONDAY THROUGH FRIDAY/...

Short Term...VFR today with light winds. MVFR ceilings will 

trend into the region this evening following increasing 

cloudiness this afternoon. Winds will also increase this evening

and overnight. Can't rule out some gusts to 25 or 30 kt along

the ME and NH coasts, with LLWS possible towards terminals near

the mountains.



IFR ceilings increase late tonight into early Tuesday with RA.

Confidence is greatest these IFR conditions pull in away from 

the coast, but can't rule out some SCT or BKN periods of IFR 

for southern NH and coastal ME terminals.



Improvement to MVFR/VFR Tuesday for terminals outside of the

mountains. Locations like HIE and LEB may continue these

restrictions through the day Tuesday as winds shift W and remain

breezy.





Long Term...Post frontal winds Wed will leave areas south of 

the mtns VFR while north and west of the higher terrain remains 

MVFR CIGs and occasional SHRA. Those west northwest winds will 

remain gusty at times during the day...up to 25 kt for all 

terminals...except where clouds limit strong mixing. Next chance

for precip around Thu or Fri remains very low confidence...but

there is a low chance...around 20 percent...of IFR conditions in

rain or snow.



&&



.MARINE...

Short Term...High pressure passes overhead and exits this

afternoon. Southerly return flow increase late this

afternoon/evening/overnight. SCA condition arrive around

midnight, with Gale conditions possible early Tuesday morning

for the outer waters from Casco Bay north. The period of Gale

rated winds may be brief within this window, but some gusts 40

to 45 kt may be possible. These slacken and turn W through 

Tuesday, but will likely remain SCA- worthy into Tuesday 

evening with waves 5 to 6 ft.





Long Term...Westerly gusts near gale force will be possible

again Wed...especially north of Port Clyde. SCA conditions will

linger into Thu...even as winds and seas diminish. Another trof

will cross the region late in the week...but storm track and

evolution is very low confidence and for now the multi-model

consensus blend does not include SCA conditions.



&&



.GYX WATCHES/WARNINGS/ADVISORIES...

ME...None.

NH...None.

MARINE...Gale Watch from late tonight through Tuesday afternoon for 

     ANZ150-152.

     Small Craft Advisory from 1 AM to 7 PM EST Tuesday for ANZ151-

     153-154.



&&



$$



NEAR TERM...Cornwell

SHORT TERM...Cornwell

LONG TERM...Legro

AVIATION...Cornwell/Legro

MARINE...Cornwell/Legro

Weather Summary for Maine and New Hampshire

National Weather Service Gray ME

715 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023



The high pressure that has brought so much fair weather will

begin to drift east Monday, allowing clouds to fill in from the

west through the day. A stronger system will move through Canada

Tuesday, leading to showery weather as it crosses. More notably

is that it will drive a cold front through the region bringing

in a cooler, drier, and gustier air mass that lingers into

Wednesday. The next chance of precipitation arrives late in the

week, and while it looks mostly wet it is worth keeping an eye

on for wintry precipitation types.

FXUS61 KGYX 061215

AFDGYX



Area Forecast Discussion

National Weather Service Gray ME

715 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023



.SYNOPSIS...

The high pressure that has brought so much fair weather will

begin to drift east Monday, allowing clouds to fill in from the

west through the day. A stronger system will move through Canada

Tuesday, leading to showery weather as it crosses. More notably

is that it will drive a cold front through the region bringing

in a cooler, drier, and gustier air mass that lingers into

Wednesday. The next chance of precipitation arrives late in the

week, and while it looks mostly wet it is worth keeping an eye

on for wintry precipitation types.



&&



.NEAR TERM /UNTIL 6 PM THIS EVENING/...

7am Update...Mainly just some adjustments to morning

temperatures. Great cooling across the interior last night with

many locations experiencing a hard freeze with lows in the mid

to lower 20s. Some stubborn stratus held on across the seacoast

of NH, allowing more mild temps there in the mid to upper 30s. 



Previous Discussion...

High pressure ridging peaks today with fair conditions and 

light winds. After a chilly night, highs today won't rebound too

much. Highs stick mainly in the lower to mid 40s as cloud cover

begins to increase around peak heating and through the second 

half of the day.



Will generally see these cloud bases lowering into the evening

amid onshore flow. The return flow behind the high will be

strong, and winds will likely be on the increase late this

afternoon into the overnight hours.



&&



.SHORT TERM /6 PM THIS EVENING THROUGH 6 PM TUESDAY/...

This flow will provide much of the area with mild WAA. Locations

in the southern half of NH and across coastal/interior ME will

see this anti-diurnal trend through the evening and overnight.

Temps may only fluctuate a couple degrees here from noon Monday

to midnight. Further warming will be possible during the late

night hours as low pressure passes into southern Quebec.



Precipitation will overspread the area late this evening

associated with this low. Overall, light QPF trend remains, and

have continued to adjust amounts down. Continue to see a

gradient of a few tenths of precipitation in central Maine to a

few hundredths in southern NH. Higher terrain points will see 

the greatest amounts, but generally fall below a half inch 

total. Rain will be the primary precip type. The only exception 

looks to be a rain/snow mix in the mountains and valleys of 

northern NH and western ME tonight. Profiles are warm however, 

and don't expect ratios higher than 5:1 resulting in wet flakes.

Otherwise, warm air should swap much of this over to a rain 

event through Tuesday.



Winds will be gusty in the warm sector overnight and into the

morning. Gusts to 25 mph will be possible in the lowlands, with

a brief visit to triple digit readings possible atop the 

Rockpile. Gale conditions will be possible over the waters early

Tuesday morning.



Much of the steady precip tapers Tuesday morning, with showers

continuing amid a W wind shift. These will be most prevalent in

the mountains. However, the cold front will come crashing

through the CWA during Tuesday afternoon. There will be a brief

period of enhanced low level lapse rates and therefore

instability to reinvigorate of showers across the interior. 

There may be enough MUCAPE for a few of these showers to contain

graupel as they pass from the mountains to the coast. These 

taper off in the mid to late afternoon with weak sun angle 

decreasing avail instability.



&&



.LONG TERM /TUESDAY NIGHT THROUGH SUNDAY/...

Overview: Largely zonal flow will keep systems moving fast and

impacts locally defined mainly by timing of each individual

wave. Reinforcing cold fronts will keep temps mostly cooler than

normal.



Impacts: With cold air nearby...any well timed wave may lead to

wintry precip types.



Forecast Details: Post-frontal CAA Wed will keep gusty winds

going and cool temps across the forecast area. Temps will likely

end up significant colder north and west of the mtns...where

upslope cloud cover will limit mixing. By late in the day or

during the evening...heights will begin rising and at least S/WV

ridging attempts to cross the region. This will bring an end to

upslope snow showers



Seasonably cool weather continues thru the end of the week...and

leads to an interesting signal Thu into Fri. The next S/WV trof

passes the area...but model guidance is all over the place in

how it is being handled. Most operational models have some sort

of flat wave that brings some rain and a wintry mix to parts of

the area. However the ECMWF EPS EFI shows a band of high shift

of tails near the coast for snowfall despite no EFI value. That

says that the top 10 percent of ensemble members are showing a 

noteworthy snowfall for this time of year. Digging a little 

deeper using DESI...the mean/median comparison of all ensemble 

members confirms what the ECMWF is showing. The mean has up to a

few inches of snowfall across the interior portions of the

forecast area...while the median is zero just about everywhere.

So it is a small handful of members dragging the mean up. So

with the threat being around a 1 in 10 chance...it is worth

keeping an eye on...but not worth putting into the forecast

currently.



Otherwise there was not much change from previous forecasts.



&&



.AVIATION /12Z MONDAY THROUGH FRIDAY/...

Short Term...VFR today with light winds. MVFR ceilings will 

trend into the region this evening following increasing 

cloudiness this afternoon. Winds will also increase this evening

and overnight. Can't rule out some gusts to 25 or 30 kt along

the ME and NH coasts, with LLWS possible towards terminals near

the mountains.



IFR ceilings increase late tonight into early Tuesday with RA.

Confidence is greatest these IFR conditions pull in away from 

the coast, but can't rule out some SCT or BKN periods of IFR 

for southern NH and coastal ME terminals.



Improvement to MVFR/VFR Tuesday for terminals outside of the

mountains. Locations like HIE and LEB may continue these

restrictions through the day Tuesday as winds shift W and remain

breezy.





Long Term...Post frontal winds Wed will leave areas south of 

the mtns VFR while north and west of the higher terrain remains 

MVFR CIGs and occasional SHRA. Those west northwest winds will 

remain gusty at times during the day...up to 25 kt for all 

terminals...except where clouds limit strong mixing. Next chance

for precip around Thu or Fri remains very low confidence...but

there is a low chance...around 20 percent...of IFR conditions in

rain or snow.



&&



.MARINE...

Short Term...High pressure passes overhead and exits this

afternoon. Southerly return flow increase late this

afternoon/evening/overnight. SCA condition arrive around

midnight, with Gale conditions possible early Tuesday morning

for the outer waters from Casco Bay north. The period of Gale

rated winds may be brief within this window, but some gusts 40

to 45 kt may be possible. These slacken and turn W through 

Tuesday, but will likely remain SCA- worthy into Tuesday 

evening with waves 5 to 6 ft.





Long Term...Westerly gusts near gale force will be possible

again Wed...especially north of Port Clyde. SCA conditions will

linger into Thu...even as winds and seas diminish. Another trof

will cross the region late in the week...but storm track and

evolution is very low confidence and for now the multi-model

consensus blend does not include SCA conditions.



&&



.GYX WATCHES/WARNINGS/ADVISORIES...

ME...None.

NH...None.

MARINE...Gale Watch from late tonight through Tuesday afternoon for 

     ANZ150-152.

     Small Craft Advisory from 1 AM to 7 PM EST Tuesday for ANZ151-

     153-154.



&&



$$



NEAR TERM...Cornwell

SHORT TERM...Cornwell

LONG TERM...Legro

AVIATION...Cornwell/Legro

MARINE...Cornwell/Legro

Area Forecast Discussion

National Weather Service Tampa Bay Ruskin FL

716 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023



...New AVIATION...



.DISCUSSION...

Issued at 119 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023

Quasi-zonal U/L pattern across the U.S. will gradually become more

amplified over the course of the week. An U/L ridge over the Gulf

of Mexico extends across the Florida peninsula. A series of U/L 

disturbance will push onshore the west coast of the U.S. during 

the next several days with a positively tilted trough developing 

over the intermountain west by mid week. This will pump up the 

ridge across the Gulf of Mexico and Florida with temperatures 

across the forecast area increasing above climatic normals due to 

the strengthening large scale subsidence over the region...which 

will hold through the upcoming weekend.



At the surface, high pressure will settle over Florida today and

will persist through Wednesday with mostly sunny skies, 

decreasing winds, and daytime temperatures gradually warming a 

degree or two each day. As the high will be centered over the 

area with mostly clear skies and light winds, favorable 

conditions each night for good radiational cooling with overnight 

lows in the lower to mid 50s across the nature coast...and upper

50s to lower 60s central and south. Overnight lows on Wednesday 

night with generally in the mid 50s north and lower to mid 60s

central and south. Patchy fog is possible mainly across the 

northern interior tonight as low level moisture begins to 

recover and the center of the surface high settles over the area.



The surface high will slide east of the Florida peninsula Thursday

and Friday with boundary layer winds becoming east to southeast.

The return flow of warm moist air will cause dew points to climb 

back into the 60s. Dry conditions will prevail under partly cloudy

skies as high pressure surface and aloft will hold over west 

central and southwest Florida through the end of the week and into

the weekend.



&&



.AVIATION...

(12Z TAFS)

Issued at 714 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023



VFR conditions expected through the period with light winds out 

of the north and northwest. 



&&



.MARINE...

Issued at 119 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023

Winds and seas will continue to subside today across the waters.

High pressure and benign conditions are expected for the next

several days.



&&



.FIRE WEATHER...

Issued at 119 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023

No watches/warnings expected. However, afternoon minimum relative

humidity values will drop below 35 percent in many areas of west 

central Florida...and several counties have ERC values of 27. But 

sustained winds will be less than 15 MPH which will preclude

issuing a red flag warning.

FXUS61 KGYX 061215

AFDGYX



Area Forecast Discussion

National Weather Service Gray ME

715 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023



.SYNOPSIS...

The high pressure that has brought so much fair weather will

begin to drift east Monday, allowing clouds to fill in from the

west through the day. A stronger system will move through Canada

Tuesday, leading to showery weather as it crosses. More notably

is that it will drive a cold front through the region bringing

in a cooler, drier, and gustier air mass that lingers into

Wednesday. The next chance of precipitation arrives late in the

week, and while it looks mostly wet it is worth keeping an eye

on for wintry precipitation types.



&&



.NEAR TERM /UNTIL 6 PM THIS EVENING/...

7am Update...Mainly just some adjustments to morning

temperatures. Great cooling across the interior last night with

many locations experiencing a hard freeze with lows in the mid

to lower 20s. Some stubborn stratus held on across the seacoast

of NH, allowing more mild temps there in the mid to upper 30s. 



Previous Discussion...

High pressure ridging peaks today with fair conditions and 

light winds. After a chilly night, highs today won't rebound too

much. Highs stick mainly in the lower to mid 40s as cloud cover

begins to increase around peak heating and through the second 

half of the day.



Will generally see these cloud bases lowering into the evening

amid onshore flow. The return flow behind the high will be

strong, and winds will likely be on the increase late this

afternoon into the overnight hours.



&&



.SHORT TERM /6 PM THIS EVENING THROUGH 6 PM TUESDAY/...

This flow will provide much of the area with mild WAA. Locations

in the southern half of NH and across coastal/interior ME will

see this anti-diurnal trend through the evening and overnight.

Temps may only fluctuate a couple degrees here from noon Monday

to midnight. Further warming will be possible during the late

night hours as low pressure passes into southern Quebec.



Precipitation will overspread the area late this evening

associated with this low. Overall, light QPF trend remains, and

have continued to adjust amounts down. Continue to see a

gradient of a few tenths of precipitation in central Maine to a

few hundredths in southern NH. Higher terrain points will see 

the greatest amounts, but generally fall below a half inch 

total. Rain will be the primary precip type. The only exception 

looks to be a rain/snow mix in the mountains and valleys of 

northern NH and western ME tonight. Profiles are warm however, 

and don't expect ratios higher than 5:1 resulting in wet flakes.

Otherwise, warm air should swap much of this over to a rain 

event through Tuesday.



Winds will be gusty in the warm sector overnight and into the

morning. Gusts to 25 mph will be possible in the lowlands, with

a brief visit to triple digit readings possible atop the 

Rockpile. Gale conditions will be possible over the waters early

Tuesday morning.



Much of the steady precip tapers Tuesday morning, with showers

continuing amid a W wind shift. These will be most prevalent in

the mountains. However, the cold front will come crashing

through the CWA during Tuesday afternoon. There will be a brief

period of enhanced low level lapse rates and therefore

instability to reinvigorate of showers across the interior. 

There may be enough MUCAPE for a few of these showers to contain

graupel as they pass from the mountains to the coast. These 

taper off in the mid to late afternoon with weak sun angle 

decreasing avail instability.



&&



.LONG TERM /TUESDAY NIGHT THROUGH SUNDAY/...

Overview: Largely zonal flow will keep systems moving fast and

impacts locally defined mainly by timing of each individual

wave. Reinforcing cold fronts will keep temps mostly cooler than

normal.



Impacts: With cold air nearby...any well timed wave may lead to

wintry precip types.



Forecast Details: Post-frontal CAA Wed will keep gusty winds

going and cool temps across the forecast area. Temps will likely

end up significant colder north and west of the mtns...where

upslope cloud cover will limit mixing. By late in the day or

during the evening...heights will begin rising and at least S/WV

ridging attempts to cross the region. This will bring an end to

upslope snow showers



Seasonably cool weather continues thru the end of the week...and

leads to an interesting signal Thu into Fri. The next S/WV trof

passes the area...but model guidance is all over the place in

how it is being handled. Most operational models have some sort

of flat wave that brings some rain and a wintry mix to parts of

the area. However the ECMWF EPS EFI shows a band of high shift

of tails near the coast for snowfall despite no EFI value. That

says that the top 10 percent of ensemble members are showing a 

noteworthy snowfall for this time of year. Digging a little 

deeper using DESI...the mean/median comparison of all ensemble 

members confirms what the ECMWF is showing. The mean has up to a

few inches of snowfall across the interior portions of the

forecast area...while the median is zero just about everywhere.

So it is a small handful of members dragging the mean up. So

with the threat being around a 1 in 10 chance...it is worth

keeping an eye on...but not worth putting into the forecast

currently.



Otherwise there was not much change from previous forecasts.



&&



.AVIATION /12Z MONDAY THROUGH FRIDAY/...

Short Term...VFR today with light winds. MVFR ceilings will 

trend into the region this evening following increasing 

cloudiness this afternoon. Winds will also increase this evening

and overnight. Can't rule out some gusts to 25 or 30 kt along

the ME and NH coasts, with LLWS possible towards terminals near

the mountains.



IFR ceilings increase late tonight into early Tuesday with RA.

Confidence is greatest these IFR conditions pull in away from 

the coast, but can't rule out some SCT or BKN periods of IFR 

for southern NH and coastal ME terminals.



Improvement to MVFR/VFR Tuesday for terminals outside of the

mountains. Locations like HIE and LEB may continue these

restrictions through the day Tuesday as winds shift W and remain

breezy.





Long Term...Post frontal winds Wed will leave areas south of 

the mtns VFR while north and west of the higher terrain remains 

MVFR CIGs and occasional SHRA. Those west northwest winds will 

remain gusty at times during the day...up to 25 kt for all 

terminals...except where clouds limit strong mixing. Next chance

for precip around Thu or Fri remains very low confidence...but

there is a low chance...around 20 percent...of IFR conditions in

rain or snow.



&&



.MARINE...

Short Term...High pressure passes overhead and exits this

afternoon. Southerly return flow increase late this

afternoon/evening/overnight. SCA condition arrive around

midnight, with Gale conditions possible early Tuesday morning

for the outer waters from Casco Bay north. The period of Gale

rated winds may be brief within this window, but some gusts 40

to 45 kt may be possible. These slacken and turn W through 

Tuesday, but will likely remain SCA- worthy into Tuesday 

evening with waves 5 to 6 ft.





Long Term...Westerly gusts near gale force will be possible

again Wed...especially north of Port Clyde. SCA conditions will

linger into Thu...even as winds and seas diminish. Another trof

will cross the region late in the week...but storm track and

evolution is very low confidence and for now the multi-model

consensus blend does not include SCA conditions.



&&



.GYX WATCHES/WARNINGS/ADVISORIES...

ME...None.

NH...None.

MARINE...Gale Watch from late tonight through Tuesday afternoon for 

     ANZ150-152.

     Small Craft Advisory from 1 AM to 7 PM EST Tuesday for ANZ151-

     153-154.



&&



$$



NEAR TERM...Cornwell

SHORT TERM...Cornwell

LONG TERM...Legro

AVIATION...Cornwell/Legro

MARINE...Cornwell/Legro

FXUS62 KTBW 061216

AFDTBW



Area Forecast Discussion

National Weather Service Tampa Bay Ruskin FL

716 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023



...New AVIATION...



.DISCUSSION...

Issued at 119 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023

Quasi-zonal U/L pattern across the U.S. will gradually become more

amplified over the course of the week. An U/L ridge over the Gulf

of Mexico extends across the Florida peninsula. A series of U/L 

disturbance will push onshore the west coast of the U.S. during 

the next several days with a positively tilted trough developing 

over the intermountain west by mid week. This will pump up the 

ridge across the Gulf of Mexico and Florida with temperatures 

across the forecast area increasing above climatic normals due to 

the strengthening large scale subsidence over the region...which 

will hold through the upcoming weekend.



At the surface, high pressure will settle over Florida today and

will persist through Wednesday with mostly sunny skies, 

decreasing winds, and daytime temperatures gradually warming a 

degree or two each day. As the high will be centered over the 

area with mostly clear skies and light winds, favorable 

conditions each night for good radiational cooling with overnight 

lows in the lower to mid 50s across the nature coast...and upper

50s to lower 60s central and south. Overnight lows on Wednesday 

night with generally in the mid 50s north and lower to mid 60s

central and south. Patchy fog is possible mainly across the 

northern interior tonight as low level moisture begins to 

recover and the center of the surface high settles over the area.



The surface high will slide east of the Florida peninsula Thursday

and Friday with boundary layer winds becoming east to southeast.

The return flow of warm moist air will cause dew points to climb 

back into the 60s. Dry conditions will prevail under partly cloudy

skies as high pressure surface and aloft will hold over west 

central and southwest Florida through the end of the week and into

the weekend.



&&



.AVIATION...

(12Z TAFS)

Issued at 714 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023



VFR conditions expected through the period with light winds out 

of the north and northwest. 



&&



.MARINE...

Issued at 119 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023

Winds and seas will continue to subside today across the waters.

High pressure and benign conditions are expected for the next

several days.



&&



.FIRE WEATHER...

Issued at 119 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023

No watches/warnings expected. However, afternoon minimum relative

humidity values will drop below 35 percent in many areas of west 

central Florida...and several counties have ERC values of 27. But 

sustained winds will be less than 15 MPH which will preclude

issuing a red flag warning.

Area Forecast Discussion

National Weather Service Tampa Bay Ruskin FL

716 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023



...New AVIATION...



.DISCUSSION...

Issued at 119 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023

Quasi-zonal U/L pattern across the U.S. will gradually become more

amplified over the course of the week. An U/L ridge over the Gulf

of Mexico extends across the Florida peninsula. A series of U/L 

disturbance will push onshore the west coast of the U.S. during 

the next several days with a positively tilted trough developing 

over the intermountain west by mid week. This will pump up the 

ridge across the Gulf of Mexico and Florida with temperatures 

across the forecast area increasing above climatic normals due to 

the strengthening large scale subsidence over the region...which 

will hold through the upcoming weekend.



At the surface, high pressure will settle over Florida today and

will persist through Wednesday with mostly sunny skies, 

decreasing winds, and daytime temperatures gradually warming a 

degree or two each day. As the high will be centered over the 

area with mostly clear skies and light winds, favorable 

conditions each night for good radiational cooling with overnight 

lows in the lower to mid 50s across the nature coast...and upper

50s to lower 60s central and south. Overnight lows on Wednesday 

night with generally in the mid 50s north and lower to mid 60s

central and south. Patchy fog is possible mainly across the 

northern interior tonight as low level moisture begins to 

recover and the center of the surface high settles over the area.



The surface high will slide east of the Florida peninsula Thursday

and Friday with boundary layer winds becoming east to southeast.

The return flow of warm moist air will cause dew points to climb 

back into the 60s. Dry conditions will prevail under partly cloudy

skies as high pressure surface and aloft will hold over west 

central and southwest Florida through the end of the week and into

the weekend.



&&



.AVIATION...

(12Z TAFS)

Issued at 714 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023



VFR conditions expected through the period with light winds out 

of the north and northwest. 



&&



.MARINE...

Issued at 119 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023

Winds and seas will continue to subside today across the waters.

High pressure and benign conditions are expected for the next

several days.



&&



.FIRE WEATHER...

Issued at 119 AM EST Mon Nov 6 2023

No watches/warnings expected. However, afternoon minimum relative

humidity values will drop below 35 percent in many areas of west 

central Florida...and several counties have ERC values of 27. But 

sustained winds will be less than 15 MPH which will preclude

issuing a red flag warning.
